    "it is quite natural to expect that a categorification of quantum groups should exist .",
    "the strongest evidence in support of this conjecture is lusztig s important discovery of canonical bases which have surprising positivity and integrality properties  @xcite .",
    "the existence of these bases suggests that the representation theory of quantized enveloping algebras , and even the algebras themselves , can be realized as grothendieck rings of some higher categorical structure where every object decomposes into a direct sum of objects lifting lusztig s canonical basis .",
    "here we show that this is indeed the case for the quantized enveloping algebra of @xmath5 .",
    "the idea of categorifying @xmath1 using its canonical basis is by no means new .",
    "it originated in the work of crane and frenkel  @xcite where the term ` categorification ' first appeared .",
    "there the authors had in mind a categorification of the hopf algebra @xmath1 at a root of unity .",
    "they argue that such a categorification could lead to combinatorial 4-dimensional topological quantum field theories . in this paper",
    "we take a step towards achieving this goal by following a suggestion of igor frenkel  @xcite to categorify the algebra @xmath1 at generic @xmath6 using its canonical basis .    prior to our work ,",
    "most progress towards a categorification of @xmath1 has been achieved by categorifying its representations .",
    "a program for categorifying the representation category of @xmath1 has been formulated by bernstein , frenkel , and khovanov ( bfk )  @xcite , and various steps in this program have already been implemented .",
    "the symmetric powers @xmath7 of the fundamental representation @xmath8 of @xmath9 were categorified by bfk  @xcite and extended to the graded case of @xmath1 by stroppel  @xcite .",
    "other tensor product representations of @xmath1 were then categorified by frenkel  khovanov ",
    "stroppel  @xcite .",
    "these algebraic categorifications were strongly motivated by the geometric categorifications of representations constructed using perverse sheaves  @xcite .",
    "progress continues to be made in the area of geometric categorification .",
    "recently , zheng has constructed geometric categorifications of tensor products of simple @xmath1-modules using perverse sheaves  @xcite .    in this paper",
    "we take a different approach and categorify the algebra @xmath1 directly , rather than its representations .",
    "more precisely , we construct a 2-category @xmath2 whose split grothendieck ring @xmath10 is isomorphic to the integral form of lusztig s @xmath0 . the algebra @xmath0 is a version of @xmath1 best suited for studying representations that admit a decomposition into weight spaces .",
    "it was first introduced by beilinson , lusztig , and macpherson  @xcite , and was later generalized by lusztig@xcite .",
    "lusztig s canonical basis @xmath11 for this algebra is such that all the structure constants are in @xmath12 $ ] .",
    "we show that all elements of lusztig s @xmath11 can be realized as generators @xmath13 \\in k_0({\\dot{\\cal{u}}})$ ] corresponding to indecomposable 1-morphisms of @xmath2",
    ".    it may be surprising that a categorification of the algebra @xmath0 is given by a 2-category , rather than a category .",
    "the reason for this is that lusztig s version of @xmath1 is naturally a category .",
    "the algebra @xmath0 is obtained from the integral version of @xmath1 by adjoining a collection of orthogonal idempotents @xmath14 , for @xmath15 , indexed by the weight lattice of @xmath1 .",
    "this decomposes the algebra @xmath0 into a direct sum @xmath16 .",
    "the collection of @xmath15 form the objects of the category @xmath0 , and the hom sets from @xmath17 to @xmath18 are given by @xmath19 ; composition is given by multiplication , the identity morphisms are the idempotents @xmath14 .",
    "thus , it is natural to expect that a categorification of @xmath0 would have the structure of a 2-category .",
    "our approach to categorification most closely mirrors the work of chuang and rouquier  @xcite .",
    "they study categorifications of locally finite @xmath5-representations using an approach that can be viewed as a direct categorification of the algebra @xmath5 .",
    "many features of their approach have analogs in our work , such as biadjointness and hecke algebra actions on 2-morphisms .",
    "this will be explained in greater detail below .      what makes a good candidate for a categorification @xmath2 of @xmath0 ?",
    "an outline of what to expect appears in the survey article  @xcite . at the very least",
    "there should be a 1-morphism @xmath20 in @xmath2 for each element @xmath13 $ ] in lusztig s canonical basis @xmath11 .",
    "there should also be 1-morphisms @xmath21 in @xmath2 for each @xmath22 lifting the @xmath23$]-module structure of @xmath0 .",
    "that is , @xmath24=q^s[b]$ ] , so that multiplication by @xmath6 lifts to the invertible functor @xmath25 of shifting by @xmath26 .",
    "we identify @xmath20 with @xmath27 and say that @xmath28 has no shift . for the grothendieck ring to be isomorphic to the algebra @xmath0 composition of 1-morphisms in @xmath2 must correspond to multiplication in @xmath0 , that is , @xmath29=[x][y]$ ] .",
    "furthermore , in order to lift lusztig s canonical basis every morphism in @xmath2 must have decomposition into a direct sum of indecomposables ; the isomorphism classes of these indecomposables with no shift @xmath30 should bijectively correspond to the elements of @xmath11 .",
    "we would also expect a categorification of @xmath0 to have rich new features on the level of 2-morphisms , and that various maps on @xmath0 ( that do not use minus signs ) should have lifts to 2-functors on @xmath2 .",
    "the grading shift operation on 1-morphisms suggests that the 2-morphisms of @xmath2 should have a grading as well .",
    "one might suspect that the homs @xmath31 should form graded abelian groups , but this requirement is too strong .",
    "in particular , if @xmath31 is a graded abelian group for all 1-morphisms @xmath32 , then the objects @xmath33 and @xmath34 would become isomorphic by the shifted identity map .",
    "however , this would imply that in the grothendieck ring @xmath35=q^s[x]$ ] .",
    "instead , we expect that the homs @xmath31 in 2-category @xmath2 should consist of 2-morphisms that preserve the degree of the source and target .",
    "the presence of the grading suggests that @xmath2 should also have an ` enriched ' hom functor that associates a graded abelian group @xmath36 to @xmath33 and @xmath37 .",
    "the enriched hom @xmath38 is a rigidly defined structure .",
    "this is because any choice of @xmath38 will descend to a pairing @xmath39,[y]{\\rangle}$ ] on @xmath0 given by taking the graded rank @xmath40 of @xmath41 .",
    "that is , @xmath42,[y ] { \\rangle}:= { { \\rm rk}_q}{\\dot{\\cal{u}}^*}(x , y)=\\sum_{s\\in\\z}q^s { { \\rm rk\\ } } { \\dot{\\cal{u}}}(x\\{s\\},y),\\ ] ] where @xmath43 is the usual rank of the abelian group @xmath44 of degree zero 2-morphisms .",
    "notice the behaviour of this pairing with respect to the shift functor in each variable .",
    "if a map @xmath45 has degree @xmath46 , then the degree of the corresponding map @xmath47 will be @xmath48 .",
    "similarly , the map @xmath49 will have degree @xmath50 .",
    "hence , @xmath51,[y]{\\rangle}= { { \\rm rk}_q}{\\dot{\\cal{u}}^*}(x\\{r\\},y ) = q^{-r}{{\\rm rk}_q}{\\dot{\\cal{u}}^*}(x , y ) = q^{-r } { \\langle}[x],[y]{\\rangle}\\\\ { \\langle}[x],q^{r'}[y]{\\rangle}= { { \\rm rk}_q}{\\dot{\\cal{u}}^*}(x , y\\{r'\\ } ) = q^{r'}{{\\rm rk}_q}{\\dot{\\cal{u}}^*}(x , y ) = q^{r ' } { \\langle}[x],[y]{\\rangle}\\end{aligned}\\ ] ] so that the pairing induced on @xmath0 must be semilinear , i.e. @xmath23$]-antilinear in the first slot , and @xmath23$]-linear in the second .",
    "hence , the enriched hom on the 2-category @xmath2 must categorify a semilinear form on @xmath0 .      in this paper",
    "we construct a 2-category that has all of these desirable properties mentioned above .",

    "@xmath94 is the algebra with unit generated by @xmath95 for @xmath96 , and pairwise commuting elements @xmath97 , for @xmath98 .",

    ". this algebra has already appeared in the context of categorification .",
    "khovanov uses this algebra to categorify the weyl algebra in  @xcite .",
    "its appearance again in the context of categorifying @xmath1 is perhaps not a coincidence . in our context",
    "the nilhecke algebra action is built into the definition of the 2-category @xmath59 .",
    "one reason for this is that the nilhecke relations help to show that any diagram constructed from the generating 2-morphisms of @xmath59 can be reduced to very simple diagrams .",
    "the nilpotency of the generators @xmath95 in the nilcoxeter algebra control the size of the collection of 2-morphisms in @xmath2 , effectively limiting the number of idempotent 2-morphisms .",
    "it is crucial to control idempotent 2-morphisms in order to have indecomposable 1-morphisms correspond bijectively to lusztig canonical basis elements .",
    "another connection worth mentioning is the relationship to chuang and rouquier s @xmath5 categorifications  @xcite ( see also @xcite ) . within their framework for categorifying locally finite @xmath5 representations they require an action of the degenerate affine hecke algebra on the",
    "2-morphisms of such a categorification . this action results in a beautiful classification theorem for @xmath5-categorifications .",
    "they also provide many interesting examples which have an action of the degenerate affine hecke algebra .",
    "our goal is to extend their construction to the graded case , categorify @xmath1 and lusztig s canonical bases , all in the graphical framework emphasizing a new interplay between topology and algebra .",
    "one drawback in defining the 2-morphisms of @xmath59 by generators and relations is the difficulty in proving that the relations do not force the 2-morphisms to be trivial , or the other extreme , the relations might be so weak that the number of 2-morphisms becomes huge and unmanageable . to show that our relations appropriately control the size of the 2-morphisms in @xmath59 we construct representations of @xmath59 built from iterated flag varieties ( proposition  [ prop_span ] ) . by restricting to the degree preserving 2-morphisms",
    "these representations provide representations of @xmath70 as well .",
    "what do we mean by a representation of a 2-category ?",
    "when the algebra @xmath0 is regarded as a category , a representation is a functor from the category @xmath0 into some other category , like the category of vector spaces , or rings .",
    "thus , a representation of the 2-category @xmath59 is a 2-functor from @xmath59 to some other 2-category , such as the 2-category @xmath102 whose objects are rings , morphisms are bimodules , and 2-morphisms are bimodule maps .    for each positive integer @xmath3",
    "we construct representations @xmath103 ( theorem  [ thm_flag ] ) .",
    "this induces a representation @xmath104 ( see theorem  [ thm_cat_vn ] ) .",
    "the 2-category @xmath58 is a sub-2-category of @xmath102 whose objects are the cohomology rings of certain grassmannian varieties .",
    "the morphisms in @xmath58 are bimodules constructed using the cohomology rings of iterated flag varieties , and the 2-morphisms are bimodule maps .    it is known that iterated flag varieties categorify irreducible representations of @xmath1  @xcite . here we extend this work to show that the 2-category @xmath58 , categorifying the @xmath4-dimensional irreducible representation of @xmath1 , carries the additional structure coming from the representation @xmath57 .",
    "this includes the nilhecke action described above , biadjointness , and the rest of the relations of @xmath2 .",
    "all of this structure is given explicitly .",
    "proving that the @xmath57 preserve the relations of the 2-category @xmath59 is a difficult task . to prove this we develop a different graphical calculus for performing calculations with the cohomology rings of iterated flag varieties . using the representations @xmath57 we are able to show that the 2-morphisms in @xmath59 have the appropriate size",
    "this is then used to show that the split grothendieck ring of @xmath2 is isomorphic to the algebra @xmath0 .",

    "recall the definition of an enriched category from @xcite .",
    "let @xmath431 be a monoidal category .",
    "a _ @xmath432-category _",
    "@xmath433 is defined in the same way as an ordinary category , except that the hom sets @xmath434 are replaced by objects @xmath435 , and composition and units maps are replaced by morphisms @xmath436 and @xmath437 in @xmath432 .",
    "a _ @xmath432-functor _ @xmath438 between two @xmath432-categories @xmath433 and @xmath439 is given by a function @xmath440 together with a morphism @xmath441 in @xmath432 satisfying the usual axioms of a functor .",
    "examples abound in the literature : if @xmath432 is the category of abelian groups , then a @xmath432-category is known as a preadditive category .",
    "if @xmath442 is a field and @xmath432 is taken to be the category of @xmath442-vector spaces , then a @xmath432-category is exactly a @xmath442-linear category and a @xmath432-functor is a @xmath442-linear functor .",
    "if @xmath432 is the category of differential graded @xmath443-modules with the usual monoidal structure , then a @xmath432-category is a differential graded category .",
    "the category @xmath444 of categories and functors admits a monoidal structure given by the categorical product of categories .",
    "a category enriched in @xmath444 with this monoidal structure is a strict 2-category and a @xmath432-functor is a strict 2-functor .    a _ graded preadditive category _",
    "@xmath433 is a category enriched in the symmetric monoidal category of graded abelian groups with the monoidal structure given by the graded tensor product .",
    "this means that the hom set @xmath434 between any two objects @xmath445 is a graded abelian group , @xmath446 where @xmath447 is the abelian group of homogeneous components of degree @xmath64 ; its elements are the morphisms of degree @xmath64",
    ". the composition map must also be degree homogeneous @xmath448    an additive category is a preadditive category with a zero object and direct sums .",
    "an additive functor between two additive categories is an @xmath449-functor that preserves biproducts .",
    "that is , on hom sets an additive functor is a group homomorphism that preserves direct sums and the zero object .",
    "the category @xmath450 of additive categories , and additive functors forms a monoidal category with the usual tensor product of additive categories .",
    "similarly , a graded additive category is a graded preadditive category with a zero object and direct sums . here",
    "zero objects and direct sums are defined as in the ungraded case , with the additional condition that the injections and projections are homogeneous .",
    "again , we can form the monoidal category @xmath451 of graded additive categories , and graded additive functors .",
    "a graded additive functor is an additive functor such that @xmath452    a graded additive category is said to _ admit translation _",
    "( see @xcite ) if for any object @xmath33 and integer @xmath18 there is an object @xmath453 with an isomorphism @xmath454 of degree @xmath18 .",
    "given a graded additive category @xmath433 we can always define an equivalent category @xmath455 , were @xmath455 is a graded additive category with translation obtained by enlarging @xmath433 in the obvious way .",
    "a graded additive functor between graded additive categories with translation will preserve translations since there is the degree @xmath456 isomorphism @xmath457 ^ -{f(\\sim ) } & f(x ) \\ar[r]^-{\\sim } & f(x)\\{s\\ } .   }",

    "[ thm_flag ] the assignments given in subsection  [ subsec_define_gamma ] define a graded additive 2-functor @xmath103 . by restricting to degree preserving 2-morphisms we also get an additive 2-functor @xmath1056 .    we have already seen that @xmath57 preserves composites of 1-morphisms up to isomorphism .",
    "the lemmas above show that @xmath57 preserve the defining relations of the 2-morphisms in @xmath59 . therefore , @xmath57 is a 2-functor .",
    "we have also shown that the assignments of subsection  [ subsec_define_gamma ] preserve the degree of the 2-morphisms in @xmath59 .",
    "thus , it is clear that restricting to the degree preserving maps gives the restricted 2-functor @xmath1056 .",
    "the rings @xmath733 are defined over @xmath122 . however , the following result holds for any field @xmath442 with @xmath1057 .",
    "[ prop_span ] the images of dotted bubbles under the representations @xmath103 : @xmath1058 over all @xmath1059 generate the cohomology ring @xmath733 for any choice of @xmath3 .",
    "this is immediate when 2 is invertible . in that case",
    ", the counter - clockwise dotted bubble of degree @xmath46 generates the chern class @xmath1060 together with products of lower degree chern classes .",
    "likewise , the clockwise dotted bubble in degree @xmath46 generates the chern class @xmath1061 together with products of lower degree chern classes .",
    "recall that the cohomology rings @xmath733 are spanned by the @xmath831 with @xmath1062 when @xmath1063 , and the @xmath808 with @xmath1064 when @xmath1065 . without loss of generality assume @xmath1066 and write all the @xmath808 in terms of @xmath831 using the grassmannian relation .",
    "the remaining @xmath216 relations on @xmath733 are given by the first column of @xmath1067 ( see for example @xcite ) .",
    "this implies that the relations on the generators @xmath831 are in degree @xmath1068 .",
    "since the representations @xmath57 are defined for all positive integers @xmath3 , it is always possible to choose @xmath3 large enough so that there are no relations on the images of a given collection of non - nested dotted bubbles of the same orientation .",
    "[ prop_closed_bubble ] the assignment @xmath1069 induces a graded ring isomorphism @xmath1070 $ ] with @xmath1071 in degree @xmath1072 .",
    "note that when @xmath1073 we have two different isomorphisms related by the infinite grassmannian relations in proposition  [ prop_infinite ] .",
    "we sometimes suppress the dependence on the value of @xmath17 and write @xmath1074 .",
    "this implies that every closed diagram can be reduced to a unique linear combination of diagram of non - nested dotted bubbles with the same orientation .",
    "we show that any closed diagram can be reduced to a unique sum of non - nested dotted bubbles of the same orientation ; this together with the above observation that there are no relations among a collection of non - nested dotted bubbles of the same orientation completes the proof .    using the bubble slide equations in propositions  [ prop_bubble ] and [ prop_bubbleii ] any dotted bubble can be pushed to the outside of a closed diagram . using the grassmannian relations of proposition  [ prop_infinite ] all dotted bubbles can be made to have the same orientation .",
    "either this process completes the proof , or we are left with a closed diagram , possibly consisting of several components , that contains no dotted bubbles .",
    "consider the innermost diagram .",
    "we induct on the number of nilcoxeter generators @xmath527 in this diagram to show that it can be reduced to sums of dotted bubbles . by contracting each double edge to a point and disregarding orientation and dots",
    "we are left with a connected planar 4-valent graph @xmath1075 with at least one vertex .",
    "first we show that if this graph contains a loop or a digon face then the number of nilcoxeter generators can be reduced .",
    "then we show that if the graph contains no loops or digons , then using only relations which do not increase the number of nilcoxeter generators , it can be transformed into a diagram containing a digon face .",
    "loops in @xmath1075 arise from diagrams of the form @xmath1076 with some number of dots labelling each strand .",
    "each diagram reduces using the reduction to bubbles axioms and .",
    "digon faces in @xmath1075 arise from diagrams of the form @xmath1077 with some number of dots on each strand . using the nilhecke relations these dots",
    "can be moved to the top of the diagram without increasing the number of nilcoxeter generators .",
    "the first diagram reduces using the nilcoxeter relation and the second two can be reduced using the identity decomposition equations and .",
    "now we appeal to a theorem from graph theory , see for example ( carpentier  @xcite , lemma 2 ) .",
    "if a connected planar 4-valent graph has at least one vertex and does not contain a loop or digon face , then it is possible by a sequence of triangle moves @xmath1078 to transform the diagram into one containing a digon face .",
    "hence , the proposition is complete if such moves can be performed on diagrams which produce graphs of the above form .",
    "the only possibilities arise from the diagrams @xmath1079 with some number of dots on each strand . again , using the nilhecke relations these dots can be moved to the top of such diagrams producing sums of diagrams in which the number of nilcoxeter generators does not increase .",
    "the triangle move above then follows from equation and proposition  [ prop_other_triangle ] .",

    "we argue that the diagrams @xmath1084 can be written as sums of diagrams @xmath1087 whose graphs @xmath1088 are such that any walk : @xmath1089 emanating from a boundary point crosses any other strand at most once and never crosses itself . by a walk we mean a path in the 4-valent graph extending from a point through each vertex to its opposite edge , until a closed loop is obtained , or a boundary point is reached .",
    "carpentier showed that any connected _ closed _",
    "4-valent graph with at least one vertex and no loops or digons can be transformed into a diagram containing a digon face using triangle moves  @xcite .",
    "the main argument used by carpentier is the existence of a configuration of one of the two forms : @xmath1090 in the closed graph .",
    "it is argued that if this configuration is minimal ( contains no configurations of the same form inside it ) , then the second case can be reduced to the first , and using triangle moves this first configuration @xmath1091 can be transformed to a digon face by sliding all the internal edges outside the configuration .",
    "the requirement that the graph be closed is only used to prove the existence of on one of the configurations in .",
    "if any strand in the graph @xmath1085 intersects itself , or a different strand twice , there must be one of the two possible configurations in .",
    "we then choose a minimal such configuration in @xmath1085 and by carpentier s argument the diagram @xmath1084 reduces to a sum of diagrams @xmath1087 whose graphs have fewer vertices . applying this procedure inductively",
    "we can reduce each diagram @xmath1084 to a sum of diagrams whose graphs have no walks emanating from an open end that cross themselves or crosses any other strand more than once . using theorem  [ thm_isotopy ] it is clear that edges in the resulting summands can be made strictly increasing using plane isotopies so that they correspond to elements in the image of @xmath1081 .",

    "<S> we categorify lusztig s @xmath0  a version of the quantized enveloping algebra @xmath1 . using a graphical calculus a 2-category @xmath2 </S>",
    "<S> is constructed whose split grothendieck ring is isomorphic to the algebra @xmath0 . </S>",
    "<S> the indecomposable morphisms of this 2-category lift lusztig s canonical basis , and the homs between 1-morphisms are graded lifts of a semilinear form defined on @xmath0 . graded lifts of various homomorphisms and antihomomorphisms of @xmath0 </S>",
    "<S> arise naturally in the context of our graphical calculus . for each positive integer @xmath3 </S>",
    "<S> a representation of @xmath2 is constructed using iterated flag varieties that categorifies the irreducible @xmath4-dimensional representation of @xmath0 . </S>"
